B000H5TH1Q|5.0|As for De Palma, I need to review the entire catalog of his whenever I get the chance, for he (and Stephen King) helped me realize I see the world the way he does at a very young age when \\"Carrie\\" came out (I was 10 or 11). And, by the time I saw this one, I was 'De Palma-crazed', LOL. I love a lot of other filmmakers (especially Hitchcock and Kubrick), but Brian does that special 'something' that appeals to the manic depression in all of us. Plus, I love how he revels in enjoying other people's pleasures/perversions/fears/desires. With his unique visual style, and his ability to grab you from the very beginning, make Brian De Palma films 'dangerous yet seductive worlds', and I am glad to say that De Palma once again did not disappoint, and that he successfully delivered a very broad range of emotions that he takes viewers on in this film.<br /><br />I saw this when it came out, and I still remember it blowing the top of my head off! I have loved this film even more every time I view it (which is VERY often) over the years. I almost knew from the beginning where the story would take me but it did not stop me from enjoying the film and admiring De Palma's ability to trick me by making me see what he only wanted me to see, yet never hiding the whole picture. What a gruesome, poignant, satirical, often hilarious, and always remarkable movie it is. It is certainly De Palma's loving homage to his favorite Hitchcock, and not just to one but several of his movies. It is a sharp satire on Hollywood, of course, but first of all, it is the story told masterfully by the Master of Suspense, making daring use of his unique and fascinating visual style. It is a great sordid-noir film and is quite creepy at times, as well darkly hilarious, for it is a satire as well as a thriller. Be sure to watch for the scene that is a running parody of bad porno film trailers, and the 'glowing' reviews from critics! Hilarious & brilliant!<br /><br />While filming \\"Dressed To Kill\\" in 1979, Brian De Palma was first inspired to make this film. The notorious shower scene with Angie Dickinson (in full ala-nude), a 'body double' was brought in to stand in whenever it was showing Angie Dickinson from the neck down, nude. Great way to immediately throw you off balance as a viewer, symbolizing right away, don't trust what you are watching, for like a magician, at some point in this story he's gonna surprise you by making you believe you saw one thing but not another, while showing the viewer what they are seeing the entire time right before your very eyes! Vavoom!<br /><br />Of coarse this has rings and tones of \\"Rear Window\\" and \\"Vertigo\\" all through it (as well as a few other great Hitchcock thrillers, like \\"Shadow of A Doubt\\", \\"Dial M for Murder\\", \\"Rope\\", and \\"Marnie\\", which the latter featured Melanie Griffith's mom, Tippi Hedren), what better films to pay homage to???! It also has flourishes of the French, Italian, and European filmmakers that have inspired De Palma throughout as well. It has the perfect combination a psychological erotic thriller is supposed to have, all the right ingredients, from erotic fervor to dark sinister terror, from insane biting satire to leaving you breathless in despair. It's a Brian De Palma Showing...An event cause de celebrete....A classic work of film art.<br /><br />Anyways, he shelved the idea, working and writing on it between his next two classics, \\"Blow Out\\" (1981) and \\"Scarface\\" (1983).<br /><br />So, in 1984, Brian De Palma returned to the genre that only he does best: The erotic/psychological/suspense/mystery/thriller/satire. He fleshed out (no pun intended) a story only he could tell (he was initially just gonna produce it, but thank God he decided to direct it as well!).<br /><br />He throws the viewer off guard right away by starting the film making viewers believe they are about to see a good late night B-grade vampire flick, then immediately shows that it's only a movie starring the main character of De Palma'sfilm. Then, as the title of the film comes on screen, with an awesome desert background that is suddenly pulled away, revealing that it (the background) is just a matte painting for some movie backdrop. Right away, like The Magician, De Palma is revealing to not trust what you are about to see for the next two hours, even though it will be done right before your very eyes. The tagline was perfect for this film: \\"Don't believe everything you see\\".<br /><br />Jake Scully, our main character (played to perfection by Craig Wasson) is a claustrophobic, soon-to-be-out-of-work actor, who goes home after a bad day's shoot just to find his girlfriend in bed with someone else! And, if wonders never cease, the apartment is hers, so he goes packing.<br /><br />From staying with a friend, a local bartender, then moving through treacherous auditions (when he already \\"is working now, and that's what matters, isn't it?\\"), to have the skies depart when he befriends a chap between acting auditions and acting class, which plays out like Acting 101, with a 'psychiatric' acting teacher whose methods just may or may not be helpful or harmful, which one???! A very crucial scene there where Jake is told \\"You must act!\\", De Palma's way or reminding his audience that they must 'live', not just be a couch potato watching life go by, participate, act! And, then things get even better for Jake (this is his lucky day, let me tell you, LOL!), his new friend (played by the great Gregg Henry) is called away for an acting gig out of town, so he needs Jake to housesit the house he's subletting. Using a real house in L.A., it is beautifully built, shaped like a spaceship, and very high in the air, with windows all around it, brilliantly filmed. AWESOME!<br /><br />Then Jake is told and shown that his next door neighbor likes to do an erotic dance every night in front of her window, in full view of Jake and the handy telescope that is set in that sole position, aimed right at her house. And, Jake, being a person of very low self esteem, and just feeling he's back in the 'world', even though it's not a world to brag about. He IS living in L.A's dirty underbelly, getting only bit parts in lowrate, B-grade (possibly direct to video?) obscure films, but he lets his esteem and obsession for a better life get in the way, seeking solace by watching the lady next door do a very sexy striptease for two nights in a row, and even while she's sleeping (he knows when you're awake, ha-ha) he still likes to peep in on her, thus noticing at some point that someone else is also watching her.<br /><br />So, in a fanatic/obsessive/compulsive way, he starts to follow Gloria Revelle (played by the beautiful/talented Deborah Shelton), the lady that lives in the house across from his. It is here that De Palma really shines with his technique of 'pure cinema', 'visual storytelling', making use of extremely long takes, and long scenes, with no dialogue, lasting for over 20 minutes.<br /><br />There then is a seduction more wonderous than the clouds outside. Yes, there is such a thing as love at first sight! Gloria and Jake are similar in several ways. Both are claustrophobic, but in completely seperate terms of the word. Both live in a world of fear, dread, depression, despair, loneliness, in a seedy world of decadence, the beautifully filmed L.A. A very sinister, corrupt city if there ever was one, especially in the movie business, and/or the life of 'The Idle Rich'.<br /><br />Jake then is plunged in to a world of hapless terror while he witnesses a murder, but is 'paralized', and can't 'act' to save the victim. He tries, lord knows he tries!<br /><br />A brief appearance by the great Guy Boyd as a very 'noirish', been-there-seen-that-world-weary-wise-guy detective, who really drills (again, no pun intended) Scully like the victim got drilled to death.<br /><br />Cut to Jake in a spinning bed, watching late night porno ads, and a very particular one catches his eye, \\"Holly Does Hollywood\\". He calls, gets an audition for the next \\"Holly\\" flick, reads for the director, gets the job.?.?. What is Jake so suddenly obsessed with now? WHO is Jake suddenly obsessed with now? Porno actress Holly Body (played by Melanie Griffith in her BEST role EVER), a naive (?), blue-eyed, bleach blonde, brain dead bimbo (?); or is she a very intelligent, extremely beautiful, rough and tough (?) femme fatale that Jake shouldn't be getting involved with???!<br /><br />One of Craig's best scenes as Jake are during this period, especially in the porn flick, when he walks into the bathroom, saying \\"Ok\\" with such a stilted slur, JUST like real porno...VERY BAD dialogue! Or, dialogue done VERY BADLY!<br /><br />Frankie Goes To Hollywood deliver a tour-de-force performance in this crucial point of the film (as great as The Yardbirds in Antonioni's \\"Blow Up\\"!) remaining as fresh today as it did then.<br /><br />Eventually the mystery is solved, super dog kills the bad man, and we have The End! But, not so easy as all that. This is a very deep, disturbing, hypnotic, visceral, cerebral look inside the Human mind, and the wicked world of Hollywood. The sleazy-ness of it all. And, the blood and gore behind the scenes. And, Jake must learn to (literally) 'act'.<br /><br />The way De Palma catches 'claustrophobia' visually is utterly breathtaking, and SO realistic. The journey into Jake's mind is a cinema sweep of pure genius! And, all over a body double.<br /><br />This is a film that will play you like a fool, but treat like its best friend at the same time. De Palma, of coarse, had to take on the MPAA in defense of the rating of this film. Plus, he originally wanted to cast a real life porno actress as Holly Body, but the studios shot him down on that one, but in his favor really, because this was the role Melanie Griffith was born to play! He first fought them over ratings in 80 over \\"Dressed To Kill\\", then in 83 over \\"Scarface\\", winning all three times. 0316044695|5.0|There haven't been many firsthand accounts written about what's going on in Afghanistan (at least that I've found readily available), making this story all the more important to anyone who wants to form an opinion of the war, either one way or the other. I daresay it should be required reading, so that people who voice their opinions on war, or Afghanistan in general can at least do so with the firsthand knowledge one gains from reading this book. In addition to describing the events of operation Redwing, and the book being part autobiograhical, Luttrell pays a beautiful homage to his fallen comrades, filled with all of the emotion and pain of someone losing his closest relative.    The first half of the book is autobiographical. Luttrell talks about his life growing up, including his motivation for joining the Navy SEALs, and more interestingly (because I know little about the military) his training at BUD/s. Admittedly the tone he takes is one of arrogance, but that arrogance is put into context when he talks about his training, and the astounding dropout rate amongst potential SEAL recruits.    The story I found to be intensely human; one of survival at it's darkest (I was reading the book at work, and had to stop for fear I might start crying, opting to instead finish the book in the quiet of my own bedroom). But for all of it's sadness, the story had an ending that was uplifing, giving one a sense of hope about the future of that poor country. I felt that I was right there with the author, suffering alongside him, losing hope as he was clinging to the side of the mountain in pitch-black after his friends were killed, thinking the military thought the same of him.    And through his brash SEAL attitude, he does raise some interesting moral questions regarding ROE (rules of engagement) especially when the nature of your mission is one of stealth, and you're literally surrounded by people who would give nothing more than to see you suffer before you die.    It's abook, one of a few writen in modern times, that I think can form the basis of understanding of modern warfare. I think it's fair to say that the days of \\"good guys\\" versus \\"bad guys\\" ended long ago, thus changing the very nature of conflict in foreign lands. In short, I think this is how wars will be fought from now on. Not city, by city , or island by island, as it was in WWII, but house by house, or in some cases person by person, as it seems to be being fought in Afghanistan.

B004OFWLO0|5.0|No need to review the incredible music of Robert Johnson. Along with Louis Armstrong, Miles Davis, and Bob Dylan he was among the most influential American artists of the 20th century--despite the fact that his entire catalog fits on two CDs.    My review focuses instead on this reissue compared to the 1990 Complete Recordings, as good as they were for their time. That version is like standing on the porch, peering through a dirty, grease-smudged window into the room where 75 years ago Robert Johnson sat in a creaky wooden chair, wailing his heart out while playing his amazing guitar with what sounds like four hands. This new set transports you into the room, sitting right next to Johnson--not just hearing the music but feeling it. There is still the crackle, hiss, and pop of these old recordings. Some future advance in processing technology might someday remove this noise while leaving all the other audio unscathed, and it's debatable whether this would be good or bad. But on these discs Robert Johnson's music comes through brighter, cleaner, fuller, and more alive than I have ever heard it.    I can't speak to whether this set simply restores something that the 1990 versions inadvertently muffled compared to even earlier versions. But I can't imagine a better set out there, and for any serious student of American music or just music period, these recordings in some form are absolutely essential. And I can't imagine being without them.

They are more like omelets than cakes, but it gets the oat bran down w/o choking.    When it comes to about 2 hours after dinner, I seem to be restless/hungry and it is time for my oat bran cakes.  Sliced cold roast, Kipper snack, boiled eggs, fat free cottage cheese for meals during the day.  Dry fried the ham trimmed of rind and any fat and spread fat free cream cheese on the slices, for dinner.      Saturday-Not too bad so far and no dizziness or weakness today.  Taking stairs slower, but not muscle fatigued, took a potassium supplement.  I recalled from a previous high protein low carbohydrate diet, that I will have muscle cramps and muscle fatigue w/o a potassium supplement.   You might also have this trouble.  Just take one a day and it will go away.   Not craving the sweets or carbs, amazingly fast, adjusted so quickly.  The best part is no hunger pain, no cravings, no feeling deprived.  I am impressed.  I have energy.  I am not bloated.  Still having a little bit of gastrointestinal distress.  Don't take the vitamins first thing in the morning.  Too hard on your tummy.  Fried ham, roast, chicken, and eggs throughout the day, eating when I am hungry.  Venison for dinner, cut any fat off, medium rare, delicious.   I put the kid's Easter baskets together today and I felt no desire to cheat and eat their chocolates, and no one was around to stop me from cheating, it was all me.    Sunday-Woke up energetic this morning, snowing outside.  What an Easter.    Dry-fried ham and warm egg yolks for breakfast.  Chicken and roast beef for lunch.  Dinner was more Venison.  Tried fat free yoghurt instead of the cottage cheese in my oat bran and egg mixture for the evening snack, did not like it as well as the cottage cheese.  Will stick with the first recipe.  At about 8:00 at night my body starts looking for that oat bran treat.  That is the only real crave for the day if I eat before I get hungry.    Monday-Vegetables today!  Yeah!  I even steamed them last night and did not snitch, though technically I could have, it being the start of my 5th day.  I went an extra day because I was feeling so well on the protein only I did not want to mess with things, but I figured I probably need the roughage so I started today.  Dry fried ham and egg yolk for breakfast.  No fatigue today or muscle cramps.  Venison with a serving of steamed zucchini and cauliflower for lunch.  Oh, last night, when I turned over to my side and snuggled my back side in to my husband and he put his arm around me to rest his hand on my tummy, we both noticed that there was not as much tummy plopping over to lay on the bed!  No scale to measure with, but less in his hands is so much better than numbers, I'll love it if I can gage this weight loss by the fit of my jeans, less muffin top to no muffin top to smaller pant size, rather than just the water weight loss numbers on the scale, that I've seen before and watched come right back...    Getting really tired of water, I've been tanking extra so that I would not hurt my kidneys, I am sick of it today.   Maybe I can add a little bit of lemon to my water, use a straw, etc., to change the delivery at least, that might help.   Much Later:  Ok, this was a miserable day.  I added the cauliflower and zucchini for lunch and I had mega cravings all afternoon.  Miserable.  I'll be glad for tomorrow, back on the all protein day.  My body remembered what it wanted and it bugged me all day for it.  Kipper snack for afternoon snack.  Cold roast spread with fat free cream cheese for dinner and 1/4 of a tomato, tasted yummy, but all that Easter candy hanging around and half of an Easter cake were really bugging me tonight, so I had the kids clear all temptation out, which has not been a problem until I added those vegetables today.   Back to my 1 egg, 2 Tbs oat bran, 2 Tbs cottage cheese cake tonight, much better than the yoghurt recipe.  As far as the exercising,  I am doing 10-30 minutes of stretching, windmills, and leg lifts in the mornings depending on my energy and strength, and in the evenings I am riding my stationary bike 20-40 minutes while I watch the nightly news when I have time and when I remember, just about every other day.  I do not have any tension on the gears so as not to build muscle, I just want to get the circulation going.  I can feel my heart beat in my extremities when I am finished for a good 20 minutes afterwards, so I know the blood is circulating.  If I start get short of breath and feel my heart working too hard, I switch exercises to a stretch and then switch back to finish my reps when it is gone.  I notice that I can do more reps the next time w/o raising my heart rate too much this way.  I have much more stamina since I have been exercising in this manner and it keeps the cortisol (stress hormone) released in my system to a minimum.       Tuesday-April 26, 2011-Muffin top not as pronounced this morning, pants not so painfully tight.  Did not unzip them in the car the minute I got off of work.  Did not run down stairs to put on my comfy sweats either the minute I got home.  Gives me hope.  My face looks slimmer to me.  I've not told anyone about the diet, don't want to draw attention, especially if I fail.  Fried ham and egg yolk for breakfast, getting sick of egg whites.  Water tastes good again today, got a straw, I know it sounds silly, but it worked.  Venison and Chicken for lunch.  No cravings today, thank heavens!  I got out a roast and some chicken out of the freezer this morning to defrost so I can cook tonight again.  Need to make sure I have lots of prepared food on hand.  This helps in the morning when I leave for work, and am in a rush, the food is cooked and ready to go w/o making me late to prepare something special, and when I get home from work, if I am hungry I don't have to wait long to eat.   Came home really late tonight and had visions of food from every restaurant we passed by, but by the time I got my oat cakes made and eaten I was craving-free again.  They must be pretty important.  Parboiled chicken and boiled eggs for dinner.    Wednesday-April 27-Day 7 starting into Day 8.  It has been a pretty painless week all considered and there is noticeable difference in the fit of my pants already, not so painfully tight that I need to pop the button to sit down at my desk.  Muffin top is noticeably less, pants pull up further in the back too.  Nice. Still not pretty, but nice progress.  Ate cold boiled eggs on the run for breakfast.  Dry-fried some slices of roast last night and cut them up into bite sized pieces and had them ready for me to grab on my way out the door, for lunch, along with a nice tomato that I ate like an apple, a bite every now and then, throughout the afternoon.   Not too bad, but sure could use a nice cold, bubbly, sugary, Pepsi... on ice or out of the can, I would not be too picky today, but I promise myself I won't cave.  I don't do Aspartame, (makes me sick) so the Diet Pepsi Dukan says I can have is out...  Too bad.  I might convert to diet if the stuff did not make me sick.  Probably better for me to stay away from anyway.  Ok, miracle.  I had somewhere to go tonight so I came home from work and cooked my oat cake and ate it on the way.  On our way home, the kids were hungry and so we stopped at a burger place and I just knew I'd cave.  We got in, they all ordered their burgers and fries and I just did not.  Honestly, the only thing I could have really swam in was the fry sauce!  I did not though.  I was amazed and I was not in pain or feel deprived.  I just was not hungry so I was good.  This is the diet to kick all diets.    Thursday-I blew it today.  Got off of work and had to run in the grocery store with my teenager.  She grabbed a box of cookies from the bakery and before I knew what I was doing, that cookie was gone!  I ate it and then another one!  Then I got queasy and kind of light headed.   Went home, ate my cold roast, lay down a little while till the dizziness (probably from the sugar) was gone, and felt sorry for myself until I decided not to kick myself too hard, just to keep going on the diet. Ate boiled eggs for breakfast, chicken for lunch.  Good day other than lesson learned, do not go in to the grocery store with teenager, before eating dinner.  Stay in the car.  Funny contrast between yesterday and today... food for thought...      Friday-April 29-Day 10-Washed my jeans last night.  Put them on this morning fresh out of the dryer and yes, the muffin top is almost gone!  I could probably stuff myself into asmaller size, but I am kind of enjoying the painless jeans for a minute.  Not needing to pop the top button or unzip them to get comfortable, is a good feeling.  Egg yolk and fried slices of roast for breakfast, chicken for lunch.  Eating less often and eating less at a time.  I think that my body is adjusting and is satiated, and I am less frantic about making sure I get enough to eat so that I won't be hungry...  all in the mental process of dieting, fearing being hungry or not getting enough.  All food for thought...  Sea food buffet for dinner, stuffed myself and had a tummy ache, but it was yummy shrimp, crab, and fish.    Saturday-April 30-Day 11-Ham and eggs for breakfast.  Oat cake in the afternoon.  Went to son's house for dinner, BBQ'd beef, sautÃ©ed onions and mushrooms, zucchini.  He also BBQ'd sliced pineapple and I caved again and had some...  Ate too much again, went to bed with  a stomach ache for the 2nd night in a row due to over eating.  Still feeling the pounds shed off.  Wish I had scales to see what the numbers really are.  Pants sure fit nice though.    Sunday-May 1st-Day 12-Roast and scrambled eggs for breakfast.  Pork for dinner.  Oat cakes.  Exercised this morning and rode bike tonight.  Got to say it is getting harder, but I think the reason it is harder is that I keep cheating.  If I'd stay off of the sugar completely I think I would not be having these doubts and cravings.  When I am good, I have no problem.  When I cave, I pay for it the next couple of days while I get it out of my system.  I think that is the reason for complete compliance, is that it makes it easier to stay on the diet, less painful, less cravings, more doable to shut the sugar out completely, rather than try and use self control and only have a little.  My body likes it and it wants it when reminded of what it is missing.   Put my dress on to go to church and could not believe the difference.  The sleeves of the dress are not sucked up tight like they have been, thebodice is looser, I could tie the tie in the back w/o my tummy looking 6 months pregnant.  The tummy is flatter in the dress, much more attractive.  I may even dig deeper in my closet and find a smaller dress for next week, just to see...      Monday-May 2nd-Day 13-Wore a shirt today that I could not have worn last week due to the buttons gaping and the form/shadow of the muffin top poking out over my jeans.  I wear larger, thick fabric tops with jackets to layer the look and hide the fat rolls.  I never wear knit tops.  Too much pride I guess, but I don't want anyone to see what I look like under my \\"layers\\".  Because I dress to camouflage, no one has noticed that I have lost any weight except for my husband and he has definitely noticed.   I am glad that fat can be camouflaged, but it will be so nice when  I can wear one shirt at a time or even a knit top again.  Yes it will be nice.  Pork, beef, and chicken cubed in a bowl to eat today.   It is easier on me to not get too hungry, I am lucky enough that I can keep it at my desk at work and eat a bite here and there instead of having to wait for my lunch break and wolf a bunch down to hold me over.   Still drinking lots of water.  Helps take the worry away about the possibility of kidney problems, though now that I am not drinking soda, my kidneys don't cramp up like they used to, so that is a good sign.  Don't know if I'll come out of this with the resolve to never drink soda again, I do love it... we will have to see how much I want to feel good and stay thin when all is said and done...    Poached salmon for dinner.    Tuesday-May 3rd-Day 14-I made it!  I can't believe it was 2 weeks ago that I said I'd try this for 2 weeks and that I'd know if it was going to do anything and here I am, 2 weeks later and it is going to work!  I am now officially excited, couldn't really get excited before because I did not want to be sad if it did not work.  The drill is simple, no fuss.  Make sure you always have plenty of meat/fish/eggs already cooked so you won't get hungry and blow it.  But if you do blow it, don't get too upset, just start over and keep going.  Try not to cheat because it makes it harder to stay faithful for the next couple of days, but if you do, realize the cravings will go away again in a couple of days and that you can still do it.   Don't listen to the reviews that say this is a boring diet or a dangerous diet.  They have not tried it.  This works.  You've got nothing to lose but weight.  Give it  a try.  You now know what to expect for the first 2 weeks.  I am thinking that the next weeks ahead will be the same.  I'll really have to not cheat if I want to enjoy life w/o cravings.  I am wanting to cry with joy at the thought that I have found something that will work for me.  I am 50 years old, not old enough to want to stop enjoying looking good in a nice pair of jeans and dancing the night away with my man.  I'll write an addendum in a couple of months to let you know how it is going.   Good luck.    Update May 20, 2011  I stayed on the diet for 4 weeks.  I lost an amazing amount of weight for me.  I was not being faithful enough to not have the cravings and so I was getting grouchy with my family...  I looked into fat free dressings, etc., and went on a more normal diet w/o no or low sugar and one serving of carb with the dinner meal.  No bread yet, but I do tortillas some nights, brown rice, sometimes pasta, and potatoes.  You cannot eat bread and expect to lose weight.  2 pieces of bread a day will maintain your weight, more than that and you will gain.  Lots and lots of vegetables and meat all through the day so my body thinks that it is a time of feast instead of famine.  No skipping meals. I am not drinking Pepsi at all, and with no cravings.  The diet jump started my system into using fat for energy instead of sugar, cleared my system of all the sugar I had been living on, and I am still losing weight with an amazing speed. I am so excited, grateful, almost in tears over the change in my body.  It is starting to look more like me each day.   When I quit the diet, I figured that I would start it again in a month, but I have not had to, as I am still losing weight.  The diet just gave me some common sense, shocked my system out of the rut I was in.  Do it.  You won't regret it.   I have been able to slowly increase the time I spend stretching in the morning and the amount of repetitions of the windmills and leg lifts and time I spend stretching.  My physical strength is increasing, and my stamina.  Still too muddy to walk, but the stationary bike works.  I have no desire to build bulk, I am stretching to make a long lean torso and working the thighs and but areas to get rid of the fat.  The fat is coming off all of me, evenly, but since the butt and legs are bigger I am targeting them.  The belly fat insulin ring melted away once I got off of the sugar.  You don't have to suffer with the exercising, just start slow and build up as you can.  No reason to hurt and be washed out for the day.  Good luck.
B003F3PMYI|5.0|I should state up front that this book is excellent and not geared towards the information technology profession directly.  However, I feel it is important to tackle this review from an Information Technologist's perspective, as I believe there is a growing epidemic that faces the IT profession.  This book made a difference for me:    As an Information Technology professional, I have watched in disbelief as many of my colleagues and co-workers have been overcome by job burnout.  The unsettling thing is that these are promising and intelligent individuals that have been forced into capitulation by the ever-growing pressures of the Information Technology role in the enterprise.  Why?  Why is it that the once most passionate and promising upstarts not only leave the company, but leave the field entirely!  The curiosity that ensued has taken my journey towards finding ways to increase job satisfaction within the information technology profession.  I am a doctoral student that has explored flexible work arrangements, such as telecommuting and work/life balance through the very real topic of workplace bullying or mobbing.  The concepts of positive psychology are more than simply a half-full versus a half-empty proposition.  Shawn Achor absolutely nails it in this book, and presents the information in an entertaining and informative manner.    I applied Shawn Achor's perspectives and have discovered that success does truly revolve around happiness, and not the other way around.  From the information technology perspective, the most influential principles that resonated to me were principle #5 (the Zorro Circle) and principle #3 (the Tetris Effect).  However, application of each of the principles can be made towards one's outlook and perspective.  For those practitioners that are pressured with long, impossible hours and neglect the social circle that surrounds you, please read principle #7 (Social Investment).  The parable that Shawn explains with volunteer firefighting issuccinct and memorable.    You owe it to yourself to take a weekend and just read it.
